## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (single-species growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt (population growth rate) as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for single-population differential-equation models in population ecology. Typical relationships encode density dependence (crowding), intrinsic growth, Allee effects at low density, harvesting/immigration terms, and seasonal/time-varying rates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita growth rate)
- Time-varying intrinsic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow trend in per-capita rate due to environment/management changes)
- Density-independent input (immigration/stocking): dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (baseline inflow plus proportional reproduction)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (c1 < 0 models constant offtake; c1 > 0 constant stocking)
- Linear density dependence (carrying-capacity in per-capita form): dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P) (per-capita growth decreases linearly with P; c1 < 0)
- Logistic differential equation (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (equivalent to rP(1-P/K) with c1 < 0)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized crowding strength; c2 tunes how sharply density dependence increases)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (density dependence proportional to log P; often used for tumor/microbial/eco growth)
- Allee effect (strong Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (negative growth below a threshold; combines low-density and crowding effects)
- Logistic with constant-yield harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (harvest/stocking added to logistic dynamics)
- Logistic with proportional harvest (effort): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * P (catch proportional to population size; c2 < 0)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity (via density term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) * P) (resources/carrying capacity fluctuate in time)
- External shock/management pulse (smooth step): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * tanh(c2 * t + c3) (gradual regime shift in net growth due to intervention or climate shift)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth analysis: writing dP_dt = P * g(P,t) often reveals mechanisms; g decreasing with P indicates crowding/density dependence.
- Crowding limitation: negative quadratic or higher-order terms in P (e.g., P^2, P^(1+c)) represent increasing competition as density rises.
- Carrying capacity signatures: existence of a positive nonzero equilibrium where dP_dt = 0, typically from factors like (1 + c1 * P) with c1 < 0.
- Allee effects: factors that change sign at low P (e.g., (c2 * P - 1)) create a critical threshold below which growth is negative.
- Harvesting/management: additive negative constants shift equilibria and can create extinction thresholds; proportional removal adds negative linear-in-P terms.
- Gompertz-type regulation: log(c * P) in the per-capita rate implies regulation is weak at small P and strengthens as P grows multiplicatively.
- Seasonality/environmental forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t in coefficients (growth rate or density term) produces periodic growth/decline and can yield oscillatory transients without explicit predator-prey terms.
- Regime shifts: smooth step functions in t (e.g., tanh(c*t)) indicate abrupt but continuous changes in underlying parameters (policy, habitat change).
- Equilibrium stability cues: if ∂(dP_dt)/∂P evaluated at an equilibrium is negative, that equilibrium tends to be stable (useful for interpreting fitted forms).

Fitted params       : c0=-1.0356e-02, c1=7.4617e+00, c2=2.6895e+01, c3=4.5872e-01, c4=1.6756e-01, c5=1.5084e+01, c6=1.3236e-01, c7=-3.3318e+01, c8=3.3523e+01, c9=-4.4277e-02

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG11)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P*exp(-c6*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) can be rewritten as a sum of three *independent functional types*:
- Polynomial in \(P\): \(0.7124493718672418\,(1-P/68.90600928530216)\,P = aP - bP^2\) with \(a=0.7124493718672418\), \(b=0.7124493718672418/68.90600928530216\neq 0\).
- Fractional power term: \(0.7124493718672418\,P^{1/3}\) (independent of \(t\)).
- Exponential-in-\(t\) term multiplied by \(P\): \(0.7124493718672418\,P\,e^{-0.03459335742983884\,t}\).

So any matching candidate must be able (by parameter choice) to produce simultaneously:
1) both \(P\) and \(P^2\) terms with *constant coefficients* (no \(t\)-dependence),
2) a \(P^{1/3}\) term (not \(P^{1/4}\), not \(\log P\), not \(e^{kP}\)),
3) a \(P e^{-kt}\) term (not \(e^{kt}\) alone, not \(t e^{kt}\), not \(e^{kt}/(c+t)\), etc. unless it can simplify exactly to \(P e^{-kt}\)).

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–3
All have structure \(P^2 c0 + P\cdot c1/\sqrt{c2+t} + (\text{something in }P) + (\text{something in }t) + c8 e^{c9 t}\).
- The \(P\) coefficient is \(c1/\sqrt{c2+t}\), which depends on \(t\) unless \(c1=0\). But GT needs a nonzero constant \(P\) coefficient \(a\). So impossible.
- Also none can produce \(P^{1/3}\): candidate 1 has \(\log(Pc4+1)\), 2 has \(e^{Pc4}\), 3 has \(P^{c3}c4\) (this could make \(P^{1/3}\) by setting \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.712...\)), but the fatal \(P/\sqrt{c2+t}\) issue remains.
Conclusion: 1–3 cannot match.

### Candidates 4–50 (all the “\(P^{1/4}\)” rational-in-\(t\) families)
Every one of candidates 4–50 contains \(P^{1/4}\) terms (either \(P^{1/4}\) alone, or multiplied by \(t/(c0+t)\), or \(c0/(c0+t)\), etc.).
- GT contains **no** \(P^{1/4}\) dependence at all. The only fractional power is \(P^{1/3}\).
- In these candidates, the exponent \(1/4\) is hard-coded (not a parameter), and the \(P^{1/4}\) term(s) have fixed coefficient 1 or fixed rational-in-\(t\) coefficient; you cannot eliminate them by choosing constants (there is no multiplicative free parameter in front of the standalone \(P^{1/4}\) in most, and even when split into two pieces, they sum to \(P^{1/4}\) identically, e.g. \(P^{1/4}c0/(c0+t)+P^{1/4}t/(c0+t)=P^{1/4}\)).
Therefore, all candidates 4–50 already fail because they inevitably produce a nonzero \(P^{1/4}\) component for generic \(P\), while GT does not.

Even ignoring that, they also generally make the \(P\) and \(P^2\) coefficients depend on \(t\) via division by \((c0+t)\) or \((c1+t)\), whereas GT’s \(P\) and \(P^2\) coefficients are constants. Setting those coefficients to zero would remove needed GT terms.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG11)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4 + c5*P*exp(-c6*t)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.7124*P*(1 - P/68.906) + 0.7124*P^(1/3) + 0.7124*P*exp(-0.03459*t)`

Expanding: `0.7124*P - 0.01034*P² + 0.7124*P^(1/3) + 0.7124*P*exp(-0.03459*t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. **P** (linear in P)
2. **P²** (quadratic in P)
3. **P^(1/3)** (cube root of P)
4. **P·exp(-αt)** (P times decaying exponential in t)

Now let me analyze the candidates. Most candidates (4-50) use **P^(1/4)** instead of **P^(1/3)**. Since P^(1/4) and P^(1/3) are linearly independent functions, they cannot match. This immediately eliminates candidates 4-50.

Let me verify candidates 1-3 carefully:

### Candidate 1:
`P²·c0 + P·c1/√(c2+t) + c3·log(P·c4+1) + c5·log(c6·t+1) + c7 + c8·exp(c9·t)`

GT needs P^(1/3), but this has log(P·c4+1). These are different basis functions - log vs power law. Also GT needs P·exp(αt), but this has P/√(c2+t) which is fundamentally different. **NO MATCH.**

### Candidate 2:
`P²·c0 + P·c1/√(c2+t) + c3·exp(P·c4) + c5·log(c6·t+1) + c7 + c8·exp(c9·t)`

Has exp(P·c4) instead of P^(1/3), and P/√(t) instead of P·exp(αt). Even setting c4=0 makes exp(P·c4)=1 (constant), losing the P^(1/3) term. **NO MATCH.**

### Candidate 3:
`P²·c0 + P·c1/√(c2+t) + P^c3·c4 + c5·log(c6·t+1) + c7 + c8·exp(c9·t)`

This has P^c3 which can be P^(1/3) by setting c3=1/3. ✓
Has P² ✓
But for the P·exp(-αt) term: GT has P·exp(-αt), but candidate has P/√(c2+t). These are fundamentally different functions of t. P/√(c2+t) is a power-law decay, not exponential decay. They cannot be equal for all t.

The candidate also has log(c6·t+1) and exp(c9·t) as t-dependent terms (without P), but GT needs P·exp(-αt) which couples P and t. The only P-t coupling here is P/√(c2+t), which can't match P·exp(-αt).

Could we set c1=0 to eliminate P/√(c2+t)? Then we lose the P·exp(-αt) term entirely. The remaining terms exp(c9·t) and log(c6·t+1) don't involve P, so they can't produce P·exp(-αt). **NO MATCH.**

### Candidates 4-50:
All use P^(1/4) as a basis function. The GT requires P^(1/3). Since P^(1/4) ≠ P^(1/3) (they are linearly independent), none of these can match. **NO MATCH for all.**
